<p>The meninges refer to the membranous coverings of the brain and spinal cord. There are three layers of meninges, known as the dura mater, arachnoid mater and pia mater.</p>
<p>These coverings have two major functions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Provide a supportive framework for the cerebral and cranial vasculature.</li>
<li>Acting with cerebrospinal fluid to protect the CNS from mechanical damage.</li>
</ul>
<p>The meninges are often involved cerebral pathology, as a common site of infection (meningitis), and intracranial bleeds.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-87589209.jpeg" alt="img-142.jpeg"></p>
<p>Fig 1 - Overview of the meninges, and their relationship to the skull and brain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dura-mater">Dura Mater<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dura-mater" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The dura mater is the outermost layer of the meninges, lying directly underneath the bones of the skull and vertebral column. It is thick, tough and inextensible.</p>
<p>Within the cranial cavity, the dura contains two connective tissue sheets:</p>
<ul>
<li>Periosteal layer - lines the inner surface of the bones of the cranium.</li>
<li>Meningeal layer - deep to the periosteal layer inside the cranial cavity. It is the only layer present in the vertebral column.</li>
</ul>
<p>Between these two layers, the dural venous sinuses are located. They are responsible for the venous vasculature of the cranium, draining into the internal jugular veins.</p>
<p>In some areas within the skull, the meningeal layer of the dura mater folds inwards as dural reflections. They partition the brain, and divide the cranial cavity into several compartments. For example, the tentorium cerebelli divides the cranial cavity into supratentorial and infratentorial compartments.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The dura mater receives its own vasculature; primarily from the middle meningeal artery and vein. It is innervated by the trigeminal nerve (V1, V2 and V3).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arachnoid-mater">Arachnoid Mater<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arachnoid-mater" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The arachnoid mater is the middle layer of the meninges, lying directly underneath the dura mater. It consists of layers of connective tissue, is avascular, and does not receive any innervation.</p>
<p>Underneath the arachnoid is a space known as the sub-arachnoid space. It contains cerebrospinal fluid, which acts to cushion the brain. Small projections of arachnoid mater into the dura (known as arachnoid granulations) allow CSF to re-enter the circulation via the dural venous sinuses.
<img src="assets/images/image-20251210-64194f92.jpeg" alt="img-143.jpeg"></p>
<p>Fig 2 - Coronal section of the skull, meninges and cerebrum. An arachnoid granulation is visible in the centre</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pia-mater">Pia Mater<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pia-mater" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The pia mater is located underneath the sub-arachnoid space. It is very thin, and tightly adhered to the surface of the brain and spinal cord. It is the only covering to follow the contours of the brain (the gyri and fissures).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-6279f5cb.jpeg" alt="img-144.jpeg"></p>
<p>Like the dura mater, it is highly vascularised, with blood vessels perforating through the membrane to supply the underlying neural tissue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ventricles-of-the-brain-and-cerebrospinal-fluid">Ventricles of the brain and Cerebrospinal fluid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ventricles-of-the-brain-and-cerebrospinal-fluid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The ventricular system is a set of communicating cavities within the brain. These structures are responsible for the production, transport and removal of cerebrospinal fluid, which bathes the central nervous system.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-ventricles-of-the-brain">The Ventricles of the Brain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-ventricles-of-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The ventricles are structures that produce cerebrospinal fluid, and transport it around the cranial cavity. They are lined by ependymal cells, which form a structure called the choroid plexus. It is within the choroid plexus that CSF is produced.</p>
<p>Embryologically, the ventricular system is derived from the lumen of the neural tube.
<img src="assets/images/image-20251210-6f696388.jpeg" alt="img-145.jpeg"></p>
<p>Fig 1.0 - Bird's eye view of a cast of the ventricular system of the brain.
In total, there are four ventricles; right and left lateral ventricles, third ventricle and fourth ventricle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043">2 &lt;br&gt; MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY &lt;br&gt; Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad &lt;br&gt; Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lateral-ventricles">Lateral Ventricles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lateral-ventricles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The left and right lateral ventricles are located within their respective hemispheres of the cerebrum. They have 'horns' which project into the frontal, occipital and temporal lobes. The volume of the lateral ventricles increases with age.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="third-ventricle">Third Ventricle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-ventricle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The lateral ventricles are connected to the third ventricle by the foramen of Monro. The third ventricle is situated in between the right and the left thalamus. The anterior surface of the ventricle contains two protrusions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Supra-optic recess - located above the optic chiasm.</li>
<li>Infundibular recess - located above the optic stalk.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fourth-ventricle">Fourth Ventricle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fourth-ventricle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The fourth ventricle is the last in the system - it receives CSF from the third ventricle via the cerebral aqueduct. It lies within the brainstem, at the junction between the pons and medulla oblongata.</p>
<p>From the 4th ventricle, the fluid drains into two places:</p>
<ul>
<li>Central spinal canal - bathes the spinal cord</li>
<li>Subarachnoid cisterns - bathes the brain, between arachnoid mater and pia mater. Here the CSF is reabsorbed back into the circulation.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-e41c6bce.jpeg" alt="img-146.jpeg"></p>
<p>Fig 2. - The anatomical positioning of the ventricles of the brain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="production-and-reabsorption-of-cerebrospinal-fluid">Production and Reabsorption of Cerebrospinal Fluid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#production-and-reabsorption-of-cerebrospinal-fluid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Cerebrospinal fluid is produced by the choroid plexus, located in the lining of the ventricles. It consists of capillaries and loose connective tissue, surrounded by cuboidal epithelial cells. Plasma is filtered from the blood by the epithelial cells to produce CSF. In this way, the exact chemical composition of the fluid can be controlled.</p>
<p>Drainage of the CSF occurs in the subarachnoid cisterns (or space). Small projections of arachnoid mater (called arachnoid granulations), protrude into the dura mater. They allow the fluid to drain into the dural venous sinuses.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-0c87ac12.jpeg" alt="img-147.jpeg">
<img src="assets/images/image-20251210-59dc93d3.jpeg" alt="img-148.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-cerebrospinal-fluid">Functions of Cerebrospinal Fluid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-cerebrospinal-fluid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-088dbb66.jpeg" alt="img-149.jpeg"></p>
<p>Fig <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>4.0</mn><mo>−</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">4.0-</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">4.0</span><span class="mord">−</span></span></span></span></span> Overview of the cerebrospinal fluid distribution in the brain
Cerebrospinal fluid is an ultrafiltrate of plasma that surrounds the brain and spinal cord.</p>
<p>It serves three main functions:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Protection - acts as a cushion for the brain, limiting neural damage in cranial injuries.</li>
<li>Buoyancy - by being immersed in CSF, the net weight of the brain is reduced to approximately 25 grams. This prevents excessive pressure on the base of the brain.</li>
<li>Chemical stability - the CSF creates an environment to allow for proper functioning of the brain, e.g. maintaining low extracellular K+ for synaptic transmission.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure-and-functions-of-the-brain">Structure and functions of the Brain<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-and-functions-of-the-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The human brain controls nearly every aspect of the human body ranging from physiological functions to cognitive abilities. It functions by receiving and sending signals via neurons to different parts of the body. The human brain, just like most other mammals, has the same basic structure, but it is better developed than any other mammalian brain.</p>
<p>On average, an adult brain weighs between <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1.0</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1.5</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1.0 \mathrm{~kg}-1.5 \mathrm{~kg}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">1.0</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">kg</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">1.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">kg</span></span></span></span></span></span>. It is mainly composed of neurons - the fundamental unit of the brain and nervous system. Recent estimates have suggested that the brain contains anywhere between 86 billion to 100 billion neurons.</p>
<p>The brain, along with the spinal cord, constitutes the central nervous system. It is responsible for thoughts, interpretation and origin of control for body movements.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad
Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="human-brain">HUMAN BRAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-060c5632.jpeg" alt="img-150.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="where-is-the-brain-located">Where is the Brain located?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#where-is-the-brain-located" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The brain is enclosed within the skull, which provides frontal, lateral and dorsal protection. The skull consists of 22 bones, 14 of which form the facial bones and the remaining 8 forms the cranial bones. Anatomically, the brain is contained within the cranium and is surrounded by the cerebrospinal fluid.</p>
<p>The Cerebrospinal Fluid (CSF) is a fluid that circulates within the skull and spinal cord, filling up hollow spaces on the surface of the brain. Every day, the specialised ependymal cells produce around 500 mL of cerebrospinal fluid.</p>
<p>The primary function of the CSF is to act as a buffer for the brain, cushioning mechanical shocks and dampening minor jolts. It also provides basic immunological protection to the brain.</p>
<p>Furthermore, CSF provides buoyancy for the brain. i.e., the brain is suspended in a layer of CSF, wherein, the weight of the brain is nearly negated. If the brain is not suspended in CSF, it would be impeded by its weight, consequently cutting off the blood supply in the lower half of the brain. It would lead to the death of neurons in the affected area</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<p>Forebrain - Largest part of the brain
It is the anterior part of the brain. The fore brain parts include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cerebrum</li>
<li>Hypothalamus</li>
<li>Thalamus</li>
</ul>
<p>Forebrain Function: Controls the reproductive functions, body temperature, emotions, hunger and sleep.</p>
<p>Fact: The largest among the forebrain parts is the cerebrum. It is also the largest part of all vertebrate brains.</p>
<p>Midbrain: Smallest and central part of the brain
The midbrain consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tectum</li>
<li>Tegmentum</li>
</ul>
<p>Hindbrain: The central region of the brain
The hindbrain is composed of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cerebellum</li>
<li>Medulla</li>
<li>Pons</li>
</ul>
<p>Hindbrain function: The three regions of the hindbrain coordinates all processes necessary for survival. These induce breathing, heartbeat, sleep, wakefulness and motor learning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad
Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="human-brain">HUMAN BRAIN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#human-brain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-055dea53.jpeg" alt="img-151.jpeg"></p>
<p>Brain diagram highlighting various parts of human brain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cerebrum">Cerebrum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebrum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cerebrum is the largest part of the brain. It consists of the cerebral cortex and other subcortical structures. It is composed of two cerebral hemispheres that are joined together by heavy, dense bands of fibre called the corpus callosum. The cerebrum is further divided into four sections or lobes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Frontal lobe: It is associated with parts of speech, planning, reasoning, problemsolving and movements.</li>
<li>Parietal lobe: Help in movements, the perception of stimuli and orientation.</li>
<li>Occipital lobe: It is related to visual processing.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol start="4">
<li>Temporal lobe: This region is related to perception and recognition of memory, auditory stimuli, and speech.</li>
</ol>
<p>The brain consists of two types of tissues: Grey matter and White matter.</p>
<ol>
<li>Grey matter mainly consists of various types of cells, which make up the bulk of the brain.</li>
<li>White matter is primarily composed of axons, which connect various grey matter areas of the brain with each other.</li>
</ol>
<p>The exterior portion of the cerebrum is called the cortex or the cerebral mantle. The cortex is extremely convoluted, due to which, it has a large surface area. The cerebrum also includes:</p>
<ol>
<li>Sensory areas: To receive the messages.</li>
<li>Association areas: These areas integrate the incoming sensory information. It also forms a connection between sensory and motor areas.</li>
<li>Motor areas: This area is responsible for the action of the voluntary muscles.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cerebrum-function">Cerebrum Function<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebrum-function" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cerebrum is responsible for thinking, intelligence, consciousness and memory. It is also responsible for interpreting touch, hearing and vision.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="thalamus">Thalamus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#thalamus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The thalamus is a small structure, located right above the brain stem responsible for relaying sensory information from the sense organs. It is also responsible for transmitting motor information for movement and coordination. Thalamus is found in the limbic system within the cerebrum. This limbic system is mainly responsible for the formation of new memories and storing past experiences.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hypothalamus">Hypothalamus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothalamus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The hypothalamus is a small and essential part of the brain, located precisely below the thalamus. It is considered the primary region of the brain, as it is involved in the following functions:</p>
<ol>
<li>Receives impulses</li>
<li>Regulates body temperature</li>
<li>Controls the mood and emotions</li>
<li>Controls the sense of taste and smell</li>
<li>Synthesises the body's essential hormones</li>
<li>Coordinates the messages from the autonomous nervous system</li>
<li>Controls appetite, peristalsis, the rate of heartbeat, and blood pressure</li>
<li>Forms an axis with the pituitary gland which is the main link between the nervous and the endocrine systems</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tectum">Tectum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tectum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The tectum is a small portion of the brain, specifically the dorsal part of the midbrain. It serves as a relay centre for the sensory information from the ears to the cerebrum. It also controls the reflex movements of the head, eye and neck muscles. It provides a passage for the different neurons moving in and out of the cerebrum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tegmentum">Tegmentum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tegmentum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Tegmentum is a region within the brainstem. It is a complex structure with various components, which is mainly involved in body movements, sleep, arousal, attention, and different necessary reflexes. It forms the platform for the midbrain and connects with the thalamus, cerebral cortex, and the spinal cord.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cerebellum">Cerebellum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebellum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cerebellum is the second largest part of the brain, located in the posterior portion of the medulla and pons. The cerebellum and cerebrum are separated by tentorium cerebelli and transverse fissure. Cortex is the outer surface of the cerebellum, and its parallel ridges are called the foila. Apart from this, the cerebellum has the cerebellar peduncles, cerebellar nuclei, anterior and posterior lobes. The cerebellum consists of two hemispheres, the outer grey cortex and the inner white medulla. It is mainly responsible for coordinating and maintaining the body balance during walking, running, riding, swimming, and precision control of the voluntary movements. The main functions of the cerebellum include:</p>
<ol>
<li>It senses equilibrium.</li>
<li>Transfers information.</li>
<li>Coordinates eye movement.</li>
<li>It enables precision control of the voluntary body movements.</li>
<li>Predicts the future position of the body during a particular movement.</li>
<li>Both anterior and posterior lobes are concerned with the skeletal movements.</li>
<li>The cerebellum is also essential for making fine adjustments to motor actions.</li>
<li>Coordinates and maintains body balance and posture during walking, running, riding, swimming.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medulla-oblongata">Medulla Oblongata<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medulla-oblongata" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The medulla oblongata is a small structure present in the lowest region of the brain. It mainly controls the body's autonomic functions such as heartbeat, breathing, and digestion. It plays a primary role in connecting the spinal cord, pons and the cerebral cortex. Also, it helps us in maintaining our posture and controlling our reflexes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pons">Pons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The pons is the primary structure of the brain stem present between the midbrain and medulla oblongata. It serves as a relay signals between the lower cerebellum, spinal cord, the midbrain, cerebrum and other higher parts of the brain. The main functions of the pons include:</p>
<ol>
<li>Controlling sleep cycles.</li>
<li>Regulating the magnitude and frequency of the respiration.</li>
<li>Transfers information between the cerebellum and motor cortex.</li>
<li>Pons is also involved in sensations, such as the sense of taste, hearing, and balance.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure-and-functions-of-the-spinal-cord">Structure and functions of the Spinal Cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-and-functions-of-the-spinal-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The spinal cord is a part of the central nervous system. It is a long pipe-like structure arising from the medulla oblongata part of the brain consisting of a collection of nerve fibres, running through the vertebral column of the backbone. It is segmented with a pair of roots (dorsal and ventral roots) consisting of nerve fibres joining to form the spinal nerves.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-cord-anatomy">Spinal Cord Anatomy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-cord-anatomy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In adults, the spinal cord is usually 40 cm long and 2 cm wide. It forms a vital link between the brain and the body.</p>
<p>The spinal cord is divided into five different parts.</p>
<ul>
<li>Sacral cord</li>
<li>Lumbar cord</li>
<li>Thoracic cord</li>
<li>Cervical cord</li>
<li>Coccygeal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad">Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<p>Several spinal nerves emerge out of each segment of the spinal cord. There are 8 pairs of cervical, 5 lumbar, 12 thoracic, 5 sacral and 1 coccygeal pair of spinal nerves</p>
<p>It performs the primary processing of information as it carries sensory signals from all parts of the body to the Central Nervous System through afferent fibres.</p>
<p>Nerve tissue consists of the grey and white matter spread across uniformly.
The smooth muscles and the skeletal system carrying nerve fibres liaise different reflexes when ventral horn projects axons which carry motor neurons.</p>
<p>It also helps intercede autonomic control for visceral functions which consist of neurons with descending axons. It is a sensitive site, which is severely affected in case of a traumatic injury.</p>
<p>Understanding the physiology of the spinal cord helps in detecting and determining the various methods to deal with diseases and damage related to the spinal cord.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure-of-spinal-cord">Structure of Spinal Cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-of-spinal-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Spinal cord runs through a hollow case from the skull enclosed within the vertebral column. Spinal nerves arise from different regions of the vertebral column and are named accordingly, the regions are - Neck, chest, pelvic and abdominal.</p>
<p>Cross-section of spinal cord displays grey matter shaped like a butterfly surrounded by a white matter.</p>
<p>Grey matter consists of the central canal at the centre and is filled with a fluid called CSF (Cerebrospinal fluid). It consists of horns (four projections) and forms the core mainly containing neurons and cells of the CNS. There are two dorsal and two ventral horns.</p>
<p>The white matter consists of a collection of axons permitting communication between different layers of CNS. A tract is a collection of axons and carries specialized information. Ascending tracts and descending tracts send and transmit signals from the brain respectively to various nerve cells across the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Spinal nerves act as mediators, communicating information to and from the rest of the body and the spinal cord. We have 31 pairs of spinal nerves.</p>
<p>Three layers of meninges surround the spinal cord and spinal nerve roots.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dura mater</li>
<li>Arachnoid mater</li>
<li>Pia mater</li>
</ul>
<p>Dura mater consists of two layers- periosteal and meningeal. Epidural space is present between the two layers.</p>
<p>Subarachnoid space lies between the arachnoid mater and pia mater. It is filled with cerebrospinal fluid.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-cord-injuries">Spinal Cord Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-cord-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Damage to any part of the spinal cord or spinal nerves results in permanent and life-long damage to the spinal cord affecting the normal functioning of the spinal cord without any replacements.</p>
<p>It often causes long-term changes in the strength, body posture and reflexing of the body. Voluntary control of limbs post an injury depends on the severity and location of the injury.</p>
<p>One has a complete injury when he loses the ability to move or sense below the injury. The incomplete injury allows the injured to perform some sensory and motor functions.</p>
<p>Spinal cord injury not only has an impact on the spinal nerves and the vertebral column but affects other muscles and vital organs as well.</p>
<p>Paralysis from an injury can be of two types:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tetraplegic</li>
<li>Paraplegic</li>
</ul>
<p>Tetraplegia is a paralysis that results in total or partial loss of use of all four limbs and torso.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Paraplegia, on the other hand, is similar to tetraplegia, except it doesn't affect the arms.</p>
<p>These injuries result in the inability to voluntarily move limbs, lose sensation, delayed or exaggerated reflexes, changes in sexual functions, intense shooting pain due to damaged nerve fibres. It also causes shortness of breath, cough and muscle spasms.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spinal-cord-nerves">Spinal Cord Nerves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spinal-cord-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The spinal nerves consist of a group of 31 nerves. These nerves are attached to the spinal cord by two roots- dorsal sensory root and ventral motor root.</p>
<p>The sensory root fibers carry sensory impulses to the spinal cord. The motor roots, on the contrary, carry impulses from the spinal cord.</p>
<p>The spinal nerves carry messages to and from the skin of specific regions of the body called dermatomes.</p>
<p>The spinal cord nerves can be grouped as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Cervical</li>
<li>Thoracic</li>
<li>Sacral</li>
<li>Lumbar</li>
<li>Coccygeal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cervical-nerves">Cervical Nerves<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cervical-nerves" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cervical means of the neck. There are 8 cervical nerves that emerge from the cervical spine (C1-C8).</p>
<p>Thoracic Nerves</p>
<p>Thoracic means of the chest. There are 12 thoracic nerves that emerge from the thoracic spine (T1-T12).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<p>Lumbar Nerves</p>
<p>Lumbar means from the lower back region. There are 5 lumbar nerves that emerge from the lumbar spine (L1-L5).</p>
<p>Sacral Nerves</p>
<p>Sacral means of the sacrum. The sacrum is a bony plate at the base of the vertebral column.
There are 5 sacral nerves that emerge from the sacral bone (S1-S5).</p>
<p>Coccygeal Nerves</p>
<p>Coccygeal means of the tailbone. There is 1 nerve that emerges from the coccygeal bone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="function-of-spinal-cord">Function of Spinal Cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#function-of-spinal-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Important functions of Spinal Cord are mentioned below:</p>
<ul>
<li>Forms a connecting link between the brain and the PNS</li>
<li>Provides structural support and builds a body posture</li>
<li>Facilitates flexible movements</li>
<li>Myelin present in the white matter acts as an electrical insulation</li>
<li>Communicates messages from the brain to different parts of the body</li>
<li>Coordinates reflexes</li>
<li>Receives sensory information from receptors and approaches towards the brain for processing.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-fd33bf34.jpeg" alt="img-152.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure 1: Anatomy of the Spinal Cord</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-reflex-action">What is Reflex Action?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-reflex-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Reflex is an involuntary and sudden response to stimuli. It happens to be an integral component of the famed survival instinct.</p>
<p>Most of the common reflexes are a response to all the well trained, accumulated knowledge of caution that we have internalized. It could be anything and ranges from the reflex action of abruptly withdrawing the hand as it comes in contact with an extremely cold or hot object. This action is termed as the reflex action. It has a subtle relation to instinct.</p>
<p>A point to be thought upon is that we all have our instincts differently depending on our past experience and understanding. A reflex is a reaction triggered by this instinct. At times, we have no prior knowledge if the pan is hot or not. In other words, instinct has little to do with reflex.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">2 MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad
Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reflex-action">REFLEX ACTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reflex-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-b2b1a460.jpeg" alt="img-153.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure 1: Reflex arc diagram</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-action-of-neuron">The Action of Neuron<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-action-of-neuron" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Two neurons dominate the pathway, afferent nerves (receptor) and the efferent nerves (effector or excitor).</p>
<p>Below is a brief description of the events that take place:</p>
<ul>
<li>Firstly, it begins with receptor detecting the stimulus or a sudden change in the environment, where the instinct again has a role to play. The stimulus is received from a sensory organ.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Then, the sensory neuron sends a signal to the relay neuron.</li>
<li>This is followed with the relay neuron sending the signal to the motor neuron.</li>
<li>Further, the motor neuron sends a signal to the effector.</li>
<li>The effector produces an instantaneous response, for example, pulling away of the hand or a knee-jerk reaction.</li>
</ul>
<p>From the above explanations, it can be clearly summarized that the moment the afferent neuron receives a signal from the sensory organ; it transmits the impulse via a dorsal nerve root into the Central Nervous System. The efferent neuron then carries the signal from the CNS to the effector. The stimulus thus forms a reflex arc.</p>
<p>In a reflex action, the signals do not route to the brain - instead, it is directed into the synapse in the spinal cord, hence the reaction is almost instantaneous.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043">2 &lt;br&gt; MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY &lt;br&gt; Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad &lt;br&gt; Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subject-human-anatomy-and-physiology-i-unit-no-iv-classification-of-peripheral-nervous-system">Subject: Human Anatomy and Physiology-I Unit No: IV Classification of Peripheral Nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subject-human-anatomy-and-physiology-i-unit-no-iv-classification-of-peripheral-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nervous system is classified into the central and peripheral nervous system. The central nervous system (CNS) consists of the brain and spinal cord, leaving everything else in the peripheral nervous system (PNS).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure">Structure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The peripheral nervous system is itself classified into two systems: the somatic nervous system and the autonomic nervous system. Each system contains afferent and efferent components.</p>
<p>The afferent arm consists of sensory (or afferent) neurons running from receptors for stimuli to the CNS. Afferent nerves detect the external environment via receptors for external stimuli such as sight, hearing, pressure, temperature etc. Afferent nerves exist in both the somatic and autonomic nervous systems as both can use sensory signals to alter their activity.</p>
<p>The efferent arm consists of motor (or efferent) neurons running from the CNS to the effector organ. Effector organs can either be muscles or glands.</p>
<p>The efferent nerves of the somatic nervous system of the PNS is responsible for voluntary, conscious control of skeletal muscles (effector organ) using motor (efferent) nerves.</p>
<p>The efferent nerves of the autonomic (visceral) nervous system control the visceral functions of the body. These visceral functions include the regulation of heart rate, digestion, salivation, urination, digestion and many more. The efferent arm of this system can be further subdivided into parasympathetic motor or sympathetic motor.</p>
<p>The enteric nervous system is sometimes classified as a separate component of the autonomic nervous system and is sometimes even considered a third independent branch of the PNS.</p>
<p>Following are the important functions of the peripheral nervous system:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>The peripheral nervous system connects the brain and the spinal cord to the rest of the body and the external environment.</li>
<li>It regulates the internal homeostasis.</li>
<li>It can regulate the strength of the muscle contractility.</li>
<li>It controls the release of secretions from most exocrine glands</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<p>Key: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">□</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\square</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.675em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">□</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<ul>
<li>= Structure</li>
<li>= Function</li>
</ul>
<p>Central Nervous System (CNS)
Brain and spinal cord
Integrative and control centers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="peripheral-nervous-system-pns">Peripheral Nervous System (PNS)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peripheral-nervous-system-pns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cranial nerves and spinal nerves</li>
<li>Communication lines between the CNS and the rest of the body</li>
</ul>
<p>Sensory (afferent) division
Somatic and visceral sensory nerve fibers</p>
<ul>
<li>Conducts impulses from receptors to the CNS</li>
</ul>
<p>Motor (efferent) division</p>
<ul>
<li>Motor nerve fibers</li>
<li>Conducts impulses from the CNS to effectors (muscles and glands)</li>
</ul>
<p>Sympathetic division
Mobilizes body systems during activity ("fight or flight")</p>
<p>Parasympathetic division
Conserves energy
Promotes "housekeeping" functions during rest</p>
<p>Autonomic nervous system (ANS)
Visceral motor (involuntary)
Conducts impulses from the CNS to cardiac muscles, smooth muscles, and glands</p>
<p>Somatic nervous system
Somatic motor (voluntary)</p>
<ul>
<li>Conducts impulses from the CNS to skeletal muscles</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-930c5d68.jpeg" alt="img-154.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure 1: Divisions of Nervous system
<img src="assets/images/image-20251210-2c78e7db.jpeg" alt="img-155.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-bfa0f391.jpeg" alt="img-156.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure 2: Location of CNS and PNS</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="structure-of-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system">Structure of Sympathetic and Parasympathetic nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-of-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system">What is Sympathetic and Parasympathetic Nervous System?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sympathetic Autonomic Nervous System: It is the part of the autonomic nervous system, located near the thoracic and lumbar regions in the spinal cord. Its primary function is to stimulate the body's fight or flight response. It does this by regulating the heart rate, rate of respiration, pupillary response and more.</p>
<p>Parasympathetic Autonomic Nervous System: It is located in between the spinal cord and the medulla. It primarily stimulates the body's "rest and digest" and "feed and breed" response.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="difference-between-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system">Difference between Sympathetic and Parasympathetic Nervous System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#difference-between-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The sympathetic nervous system prepares the body for the "fight or flight" response during any potential danger. On the other hand, the parasympathetic nervous system inhibits the body from overworking and restores the body to a calm and composed state. The difference between the sympathetic and parasympathetic nervous system are differentiated based on the way the body responds to environmental stimuli.</p>
<p>The major difference between sympathetic and parasympathetic nervous system are summarised below:</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-afc8496f.jpeg" alt="img-157.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="difference-between-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic">DIFFERENCE BETWEEN SYMPATHETIC AND PARASYMPATHETIC<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#difference-between-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251210-eca2792c.jpeg" alt="img-158.jpeg"></p>
<p>Figure 1: Difference between Sympathetic and Parasympathetic Nervous system</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy">MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043</p>
<table><thead><tr><th style="text-align: left;">Sympathetic</th><th style="text-align: left;">Parasympathetic</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td style="text-align: left;">Involved in the fight or flight response.</td><td style="text-align: left;">Involved in maintaining homeostasis and &lt;br&gt; also, permits the rest and digest response.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">The sympathetic system prepares the body for &lt;br&gt; any potential danger.</td><td style="text-align: left;">The parasympathetic system aims to bring &lt;br&gt; the body to a state of calm.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">Sympathetic system has shorter neuron &lt;br&gt; pathways, hence a faster response time.</td><td style="text-align: left;">Has comparatively longer neuron &lt;br&gt; pathways, hence a slower response time.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">Increases heartbeat, muscles tense up.</td><td style="text-align: left;">Reduces heartbeat, muscles relaxes.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">The pupil dilates to let in more light.</td><td style="text-align: left;">The pupil contracts.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">Saliva secretion is inhibited.</td><td style="text-align: left;">Saliva secretion increases, digestion &lt;br&gt; increases.</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: left;">On "fight and flight" situations, Adrenaline is &lt;br&gt; released by the adrenal glands; more glycogen is &lt;br&gt; converted to glucose.</td><td style="text-align: left;">No such functions exist in "fight or flight" &lt;br&gt; situations.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The autonomic nervous system comprises of two parts- the sympathetic and parasympathetic nervous system. The sympathetic nervous system activates the fight or flight response during a threat or perceived danger, and the parasympathetic nervous system restores the body to a state of calm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043">2 &lt;br&gt; MARRI LAXMAN REDDY INSTITUTE OF PHARMACY &lt;br&gt; Approved by AICTE &amp; PCI, Affiliated to JNTU Hyderabad &lt;br&gt; Dundigal, Quthbullapur (M), Hyderabad 500043<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-br-marri-laxman-reddy-institute-of-pharmacy-br-approved-by-aicte-pci-affiliated-to-jntu-hyderabad-br-dundigal-quthbullapur-m-hyderabad-500043" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system">Functions of Sympathetic and Parasympathetic nervous system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-sympathetic-and-parasympathetic-nervous-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Parasympathetic System</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rest-and-digest-response">"Rest and digest" response:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rest-and-digest-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Increase in blood flow to the gastrointestinal tract, which helps to meet the greater metabolic demands placed on the body by the GI tract</li>
<li>Constriction of the bronchioles when oxygen levels are normalized</li>
<li>Control of the heart via the Vagus nerve cardiac branches and spinal accessory nerves of the thoracic spinal cord</li>
<li>Constriction of the pupil allowing for near vision control</li>
<li>Stimulation of salivary gland production and speeds up peristalsis to aid digestion</li>
<li>Relaxation/contraction of the uterus and erection/ejaculation in men</li>
</ul>
<p>In order to understand the functioning of the parasympathetic nervous system, it is helpful to use a real example:</p>
<p>The male sexual response is under direct control of the CNS. Erections are controlled by the parasympathetic system through excitatory pathways. Excitatory signals originate in the brain, through thought, sight or direct stimulation. Regardless of the origin of the excitatory signal, penile nerves respond by releasing acetylcholine and nitric oxide, which in turn signal the smooth muscles of the arteries of the penis to relax and fill with blood. This cascade of events results in erection.</p>
<p>The Sympathetic System
"Fight or Flight" response:</p>
